B002ZG980U|2.0|I was going to let this review go because I got to see INCEPTION via Amazon's Video On Demand for free as part of a promotion.  Still, as an aspiring screenwriter and basic movie fan, I've got to say something here.    (If like me you hate spoilers, scroll to the bottom of this review and read the last line.  Otherwise, I proceed as if you've already seen the film.)    If you think INCEPTION is simply amazing -- you've been scammed.  I know, this is a sacrilege of modern cinema to suggest the 'genius' behind DARK KNIGHT could possibly misstep, but INCEPTION only solidifies my view that Nolan has a reality distortion field around him that Steve Job's would envy.    First of all, there is a thing known in screenplays known as 'exposition'.  Exposition is when the characters explain the story to YOU to make sure you understand what's going on and what it means.  The more time the story spends explaining the story, the weaker and more convoluted the story.  Too much exposition reveals a core flaw of a screenplay -- in that -- instead of having fun with the story, the story spends too much time explaining itself.    INCEPTION is wall to wall exposition.  It should have been called EXPOSITION it's so bad.  It never lets up, and the reason is NOT because the film is such a 'clever engaging 'mind-bender'.  The story never stops explaining itself to you is it's poorly constructed.      There are simple work-arounds to make a story present itself more clearly.  It's called a second draft.    For instance, the story uses an old device known as 'explain it to the newbie'.  The Juno actress is brought in as a newbie and the entire dreaming world is explained to her.  Piece by piece.  As it's explained to her, it's explained to us.   Get it?  You've seen it a million times.  AVATAR used it too.  The problem here:  we didn't need the explanation.    You think I'm nuts.  The story was confusing as hell and OF COURSE we needed the 'tell it to the newbie' trick to follow what was going on.  Salami.    Was the plot really that difficult to follow?  The way it was presented, absolutely, but let me prove to you how simple to plot actually was:  a team of dream re-enginners attack a sleeping son of a businessman and insert into his mind the desire to dissolve his Dad's business.  In order to implant this idea the dream re-engineers must create three dreams within a dream to pull this off, and have a matter of minutes in the first dream, hours in the second, and weeks in the third.    Isn't that basically it?  Yup.  Isn't that nice and clean and simple?  Yup.  Could that have been elegantly explained in a few opening scenes.  Yup.  Did this team need to pull in a newbie device and risk their lives on a novice?  Nope.    INCEPTION takes ONE HOUR to explain what I just explained in two sentences.  Not because it's cool and clever and wildly imaginative... but because it's poorly written rubbish.    Oh, I know, the fans of this film just shuttered.  Rubbish?  Impossible!  \\"Why this was the director of DARK KNIGHT for crying out loud and INCEPTION made a fortune at the box office too!\\"      Stop being a fanboy and ask yourself this:  was this Leonardo's best work?  When you think of what a great actor he can be, is this one of the movies you'll think of first?  I won't.      I swear he spent the entire film with the same one pained look.  Downright constipated if you ask me.  I think he was supposed to be an emotionally distraught dude hiding a 'secret' that Juno girl eventually uncovered, but that doesn't explain his one note performance.    The reason he looked so desperate and scared was that there no character to grab onto.  Leo's character was like all the characters in this piece:  one note comic book bad@sses.  Absolutely nothing more.  Pink Fluffernutter in dark suits.    Modern cinema (I just hate putting those two words together) has this scam that's in nearly all 'big' movies these days -- and -- audiences consistently fall for it box officeweekend after box office weekend.  It is:  any one of us could be a bad@ss, and when you join a team of bad@asses... wow... aren't you REALLY COOL.    The scam of a movie like INCEPTION isn't that the idea of dream re-engineering is cool.  That's actually a good idea.  The scam is that you could be one of these people -- that you're smart enough and tough enough to swagger like the idiots in this film.  That each one of us is really just a James Bond in discounted jeans.  That's what you're really being sold here.    Yes, I know, that all movies invite us into a character and give us a chance to be someone else.  But you know what?  In good movies -- in your best Bond movies -- you feel like there's an actual person there as well.   That, yes, you can pretend to be Bond at times, but at other times, you must face you're not Bond and James is.  This is why Bond can be amazing - because you must admit he's a bad@ss and you're not.    When watching INCEPTION I merely see a room of nothings running around from dream to dream.  I didn't really buy that any of these people were real or mattered.    For example, Leo cared very much about his wife.  He wanted to be with her.  Did we care about her?  Did WE want to be with her?  Nope.  Remember why?  She came off as a psychotic during most of her scenes.    The movie pulls Juno girl out of nowhere.  She was in school but was -- oddly -- ready and willing to leave it at a moment's notice.  No boyfriend or family, no fear that some insane caper might destroy her mind and body.  Did they offer her money?  Did they promise her a place in a grad school?  I don't remember hearing any such offers.  Do you?    INCEPTION isn't about really exploring this cool dream idea and making it real.  It's merely about inviting you along as a member of a team of bad@asses AND escorting you through a series of reasonably impressive CGI.  THAT'S ALL.  It's so that you can leave the cinema with a big swagger and feel cool.    You know how some people simply HATE Apple for selling cool over anything else?  That just having a Mac is cool in and of itself?  That's all INCEPTION is.  Stop pontificating about how 'amazing' it was.      It wasn't.  It was just okay at best.  Must NOT hurry to see cinema.    Still not buying this?  Think about the plot again.  The motivation behind Leo's quest.  Leo has taken a job to break up a corporation so that it's competitor can make even bigger profits.  Did you catch that?  It's not that the corporation that's being broken up is 'evil'.  It wasn't.  So Leo is really working on behalf of an 'evil' corporation that's attacking another corporation for immense greed and profit.    ... yay?    Wouldn't it simply be cheaper for the competing corporation to buy off the son instead of this completely insane and convoluted plot?  I know, I know, when you go see a fantastic movie you have to give them a little elbow room.  I did.  But INCEPTION demands a stadium of elbow room... just for starters.    Did you notice how Juno girl was amazingly perceptive?  I mean she's not just an amazing 'maze' girl, or scientific mind, but she's also a perceptive psychotherapist?  All this in a youthful package which OH SO CONVENIENTLY is a voicebox for the smarter/aged screenwriter?  Yes, I know, she's as cute as hell, but I didn't let my hormones distract me from the simple fact she was a %100 unbelievable character.    And speaking of hormones:  why wasn't Leo interested in this girl?  Or this girl interested in Leo?  Yes, I know, Leo was obsessed with his psychotic wife, and Juno girl was afraid that Leo might be a mental case.  Still, there's something in heterosexual oriented movies known as 'the love interest' which Juno girl would have been perfect for... had she been cast as an older woman.  But poor INCEPTION was so busy explaining and reexplaining the world's most unnecessarily complex plot that --    -- it has absolutely no time for a few genuinely emotional moments between Leo and Juno.(I should look up their real character names, shouldn't I?  But since they weren't really characters -- since the writer/director didn't bother to rewrite his opus -- I'll be similarly lazy.)    But the special effects were awesome, you say like a trained monkey?  Okay, alright, let's discuss two of them to put this sorry movie out of it's misery.    When Juno girl first discovers she's not on a street but really in a dream world, the entire street begins erupting.  Poof-pang-kapliff!  So COOL, right?  Wrong.  Tell me, why didn't it ever do this again when other characters were outright told that the world they thought was real was actually a dream?      I bet you didn't notice that, did you?  Know why?  You were so captivated by the cool poof-pang-kapliff effect you forgave the story for making no sense.  That it didn't even follow its own rules.    Remember when Juno girl folded the street up and over?  A really really COOL special effect... utterly wasted.  What if during one of the chase scenes she invoked it to flip the car behind them?  That would have been really SMART, right?  You know, using a skill they had to alter the situation?  The reason why they didn't do this --    -- was because the story wasn't following it's own rules.  They were shifting at the whims of story and CGI. Face it:  this is yet another special effects feast that's exciting to watch once and never again.     Overlong, way too much exposition, too many characters, all characters were Pink Fluffernutter, a stunningly convoluted plot, a hero (?) on an extremely selfish quest, a sidekick too smart to believe and too hot to ignore, a third act stolen frame for frame out of FOR HER MAJESTY'S SECRET SERVICE, and yet another story that invites you to 'be all you can be' so that you can leave the cinema feeling COOL with a BAD@SS swagger.    INCEPTION is a scam.     If you rolled your eyes at AVATAR, you'll roll them here too.

B002ZG981E|5.0|Inception is the kind of film that you either love or hate. Just head over to any movie review website and you will see this first hand. I myself absolutely loved it. The idea of entering people's dreams is certainly not a new premise in Hollywood however, with that being said, this film take the concept to completely new heights. As the title of my review states, very few directors could have pulled this scrip off successfully. It could have easily become convoluted, confusing, and bogged down with exposition. Christopher Nolan does a remarkable job and I have no doubts that is mostly due to the control he had over this film as he wrote, produced, and directed.<br /><br />I don't want to give too much away in this review so ill give just the basic premise and its actually quite simple. People can enter other people's dreams and steal information. Leonardo Dicaprio's character, Dominick Cobb, is one of the best at doing just this and ultimately he winds up being hired by Ken Watanabe's character, Saito, to enter a competitors mind but this job isn't about stealing information, its about planting an idea in this persons mind, a process called Inception. Were led to believe by many characters that such a thing is not possible yet Cobb disagrees and takes the job.<br /><br />That's as far as I will go in regards to actual details about the film as I don't want to ruin anything for anyone. Ill simply say that it winds up being one of the most complex science fiction films I have ever seen yet Nolan never loses control with this film. Everything is masterful sewn together and the experience is second to none. Everyone gives an outstanding performance especially Leonardo Dicaprio, Tom Hardy, Cillian Murphy, Marion Cotillard, Tom Berenger, and Joseph Gordon-Levitt. Tom Hardy's performance in particular really blew me away. This film would not have been the same without him.<br /><br />I simply have to mention the score as it was absolutely brilliant and ultimately its one of the best scores I have ever heard. I have to admit I was surprised when I heard Hans Zimmer was the composer. Don't get me wrong Zimmer is a master but his work is usually more predictable and his scores always seem to have a similar feel to them. His work with Nolan on The Dark Knight and now Inception have really pushed Zimmer creatively and ultimately Inception is a different kind of score than I think he's ever delivered before. In all honesty if someone had come to me with this soundtrack a couple months ago, before I saw the film, and asked me to guess who the composer was, Zimmer would have been one of my last guesses. It really is one of his most original compositions.<br /><br />Bottom line - Inception is hands down one of the best films I have seen in years. It has an amazing story, a great cast, some outstanding special effects and one of the best scores I have ever heard. In the hands of most directors this film would most likely have been a blabbering mess but Nolan's dedication to detail makes the delivery of this film practically flawless.<br /><br />5 stars!!ave ever heard. Both main characters lead lives embroiled in social and political environments that will be familiar with anyone who has grown up in the Britain of Thatcher, Major and Blair. Their stories have the universal quality that writers strive for, and I think this is why the book is so popular.<br /><br />Yes the writing is pretty lowbrow, and the much vaunted wit of David Nicholls is not particularly apparent. One particularly poorly drawn minor character Ian, a boyfriend of Emma during one of her hapless phases, relies too much on forced stand up comedy lines. But the quirky love story is genuine and affecting, and (albeit partly through a plot climax featuring a rather forced deus ex machina) many readers will find themselves welling up somewhat over the final pages.<br /><br />Not a heavy read, but good on the details of 80s, 90s and naughties Britain - the rise of 'media', the struggles of people with a genuinely left wing conscience, the difficulties of making a fulfilling living in a genuinely worthwhile career, the obsession with youth, beauty and 'self', the extortionate property prices.<br /><br />The middle brow writers that dominate the media - Tony Parsons, Nick Hornby, you know the types, have been drooling all over this book and it is easy to see why: they wish they had written it. The movie will surely follow.

0061714372|5.0|This is an odd review for me to write as I usually read and comment on historical subjects and other scholarly works (I'm an historian), but I also happen to love Megadeth.  So, I stumbled across Mustaine's autobiography and promptly downloaded it to my iPad.  What a read!  If it were not for my tendency to sleep and eat at least once a day I would have finished it in one sitting.      Mustaine is obviously a must read for any Metal fan, but it would also be enlightening for anyone else struggling through similar circumstances trying to find meaning in their own life.  I have led a very different path than Mustaine, but the parallels are there in enough abundance that his book held a deep personal message for me.  I can't imagine anyone reading this book, especially those who have gone through some of the same crap Mustaine has in his own life, not being affected positively in some way.  Mustaine does not preach for sure.  Neither does he come off as someone who has found the answers for everyone; but he does share intimately the reason for his life having significance beyond profane carnal and egotistical fulfillment, and especially the deadly road that a person's life can take not having found it.  This, I believe, is the reason for his goodness as a person and continuing greatness as musician today.      All of us classic Metalheads who have kept touch with the music of Megadeth are in awe of the material Mustaine has produced over the last several years, especially given the apparent decline of Megadeth (and Metal in general) throughout the late 90's and early century.  But Mustaine, and with him Megadeth has been resurrected to such astounding heights that even transcend the `classic' Megadeth of the 80s and early 90s.  Even the new Metal kids love it.  For all of us balding, bulging, aging Metalheads trudging towards (or through) middle-age life, the music of Megadeth gives us hope that some things do get better with age and we can sometimes outdo our youngerselves with a sharper edge and greater intensity than ever before.  It's all about focus; and that focus must be on that which is greater than oneself.     There is (not shockingly) much in this book about the Metallica-Megadeth rivalry.  From the perspective of this aging rocker (me), Metallica has been a grievous disappointment through the later years...and this is coming from someone who was long a member of the Metallica faction.  Mustaine had been for most of his career always a step behind the great monster of Metallica; but no more.  He has surpassed them.  This may not be Mustaine's opinion (he seems to still believe otherwise), but it is my own.  This book helps explain why.  I sadly doubt that Metallica will ever regain, let alone surpass the great band it once was.  Megadeth on the other hand has never been better.  Looking at it from their careers as a whole and where they are now there is little doubt amongst those of us that were fans of them both from the very beginning that in the end - Mustaine has finally won!

The light cycles have been upgraded, and you see programs disassembled and destroyed In more graphic fashion than in the original movie. Daft Punk's score is definitely another element that really made the movie quite an experience.     The performances in the movie are good.  As talked about Jeff Bridges as Kevin Flynn has grown from the original movie. He's no longer the that nave hacker with a love for computers, now he's older and seen his great creation once again perverted again.  Garrett Hedlund as Sam Flynn does his role well as the estranged son here. Olivia Wilde as his would be love interest is also pretty good.      Tron Legacy is a good sequel that definitely lives up the hype surrounding it. Studios gave the director a mighty big budget to work with, and he took advantage of it. It's true the script and story could have been better but as far as what happens to the main character of Kevin Flynn, they did answer a lot of questions that we wanted to know since the first movie and introduced a couple of new ones for possible sequels. If there are plans for further entries in the franchise then they must include a deeper story that takes more advantage of the characters from the original including Tron.  As far as this movie goes,  I think they got right what they were supposed to do which is get news fans interested in the franchise, and get older dedicated fans of  the original something to look back on.

Their stunning self-titled debut album to this day remains a strong example of skillfully composed and passionate music. Catchy guitar riffs, intense drumming, incredible vocals - you name it, they got it. Get ready for the experience of your life....<br /><br />Crimson Glory was formed in 1982 in Sarasota, Florida, back then going by the name of Beowulf. The three musicians who started the group were Jon Drenning (guitar), Ben Jackson (guitar) and Jeff Lords (bass). With the addition of Dana Burnell (drums) and Midnight (vocals) the formation changed its name to Crimson Glory and begun working on their own unique musical style. It took them four years to come up with the material which was soon released by Roadrunner and instantly received surprisingly good feedback from both critics and music fans. Surprisingly - because no one really expected such a powerful record from a young, debuting band. Nowadays compared to the likes of early Queensryche, Fates Warning and Fifth Angel, the album contained a thrilling mixture of glam and heavy metal - the songs stretched out from fast, heavy blows (\\"Mayday\\", \\"Angels Of War\\") to majestic masterpieces (\\"Valhalla\\", \\"Azrael\\") and beautiful ballads (\\"Heart Of Steel\\", \\"Lost Reflection\\"). Released in 1986, the album was truly groundbreaking for its time, and years later it can still leave the listener speechless. All tracks feature excellent guitar work by both Drenning and Jackson - violent riffs intertwine with brilliant solos throughout the entire album. Also Burnell's drumming and some of Lords' bass parts deserve applaud, but the real highlight of Crimson Glory is definitely Midnight's vocals. Compared to Rob Halford himself, Midnight proved to be one of the best singers in the history of metal music, able to easily switch between impressive clear vocals and incredibly high pitched shrieks. Songs such as \\"Mayday\\" and \\"Dragon Lady\\" are the best examples of Midnight's amazing vocal abilities.<br /><br />However, the songs featured a lot more than just solid vocal lines. The lyrics, usually concentrating on mysterious women or science fiction/astronomy themes, helped to establish a very strong mood of melancholy and sadness, in the same time losing nothing from its majestic form. The mystical atmosphere was strengthened by the band's live shows, during which all of Crimson Glory's members performed wearing characteristic silver masks such as the ones depicted in the album's inlay. With all these elements put together, no wonder their debut album became quite a success - it was a fresh breeze on the metal market and delivered a great dose of charismatic, melodic music.<br /><br />The follow up album, \\"Transcendence\\" (1988), expanded the ideas found in the debut and featured even more epic material, which helped Crimson Glory gather a loyal fellowship of fans, to whom they referred to as The Crimson Militia. Their next album, \\"Strange And Beautiful\\" (1991), was a big step forward for the band's music - the epic progressive metal stylistics were confronted with blues and hard rock elements. Although not all fans appreciated this combination, the album was still a success and proved to be a valuable part of Crimson Glory's discography. Unfortunately, after it's release the band broke up and it wasn't until 1999, when a new album saw the day of light. \\"Astronomica\\", recorded with a new singer Wade Black and ex-Savatage drummer Steve Wacholz, was a return to the epic progressive /power metal vibes present on the first two albums. Enthusiastically greeted by the fans, it remains the band's last offering todate.<br /><br />Crimson Glory have long ago carved their name in the history of metal, as their releases still dazzle fans all over the world. The band's self-titled debut proves their unique abilities to deliver fast, heavy and - most of all - passionate music. \\"Crimson Glory\\" remains one of the most fascinating albums of the 80's metal scene - if you haven't discovered it yet, this is your chance!have long ago carved their name in the history of metal, as their releases still dazzle fans all over the world. The band's self-titled debut proves their unique abilities to deliver fast, heavy and - most of all - passionate music. \\"Crimson Glory\\" remains one of the most fascinating albums of the 80's metal scene - if you haven't discovered it yet, this is your chance!
